src/servo_2040/servo_2040/serial_node.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
import serial
import time
from typing import Optional


class SerialNode(Node):
    """Base class for ROS2 nodes that communicate over serial."""

    def __init__(self, node_name: str):
        """Initialize the serial node.
        
        Args:
            node_name: Name of the ROS2 node
        """
        super().__init__(node_name)
        
        # Declare common parameters
        self.declare_parameter('serial_port', '/dev/ttyACM0')
        self.declare_parameter('baudrate', 115200)
        
        # Get parameters
        self.serial_port = self.get_parameter('serial_port').value
        self.baudrate = self.get_parameter('baudrate').value
        self.serial: Optional[serial.Serial] = None
        
        # Initial connection attempt
        self.connect_serial()

    def connect_serial(self) -> None:
        """Attempts to connect to the serial port."""
        while self.serial is None and rclpy.ok():
            try:
                self.serial = serial.Serial(
                    self.serial_port,
                    self.baudrate,
                    timeout=1
                )
                self.get_logger().info(
                    f"Connected to {self.serial_port} at {self.baudrate} baud."
                )
            except serial.SerialException as e:
                self.get_logger().error(
                    f"Failed to connect to {self.serial_port}: {e}"
                )
                time.sleep(1)  # Wait before retrying

    def write_serial(self, data: str) -> bool:
        """Write data to the serial port.
        
        Args:
            data: String to write to serial port
            
        Returns:
            bool: True if write successful, False otherwise
        """
        if self.serial is None:
            self.connect_serial()
            return False
            
        try:
            self.serial.write(data.encode('utf-8'))
            return True
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Serial write error: {e}")
            self.serial = None
            return False

    def read_serial(self) -> Optional[str]:
        """Read data from the serial port.
        
        Returns:
            Optional[str]: Data read from serial port or None if error
        """
        if self.serial is None:
            self.connect_serial()
            return None
            
        try:
            if self.serial.in_waiting > 0:
                return self.serial.readline().decode('utf-8').strip()
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Serial read error: {e}")
            self.serial = None
        return None
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

<<<<<<< SEARCH
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
import serial
import time


class SerialListener(Node):
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__('serial_listener')
        self.declare_parameter('serial_port', '/dev/ttyACM0')
        self.declare_parameter('baudrate', 115200)

        self.serial_port = self.get_parameter('serial_port').value
        self.baudrate = self.get_parameter('baudrate').value
        self.serial = None

        # Initial attempt to connect
        self.connect_serial()

        # Timer for polling serial data
        self.timer = self.create_timer(0.1, self.read_serial_data)

    def connect_serial(self):
        """Attempts to connect to the serial port."""
        while self.serial is None:
            try:
                self.serial = serial.Serial(self.serial_port, self.baudrate, timeout=1)
                self.get_logger().info(f"Connected to {self.serial_port} at {self.baudrate} baud.")
            except serial.SerialException as e:
                self.get_logger().error(f"Failed to connect to {self.serial_port}: {e}")
                time.sleep(1)  # Wait 1 second before retrying

    def read_serial_data(self):
        """Reads data from the serial port."""
        if self.serial is None:
            self.connect_serial()
            return

        try:
            if self.serial.in_waiting > 0:
                data = self.serial.readline().decode('utf-8').strip()
                self.get_logger().info(f"Received: {data}")
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Serial error: {e}. Reconnecting...")
            self.serial = None
=======
import rclpy
from servo_2040.serial_node import SerialNode


class SerialListener(SerialNode):
    """Node that listens for serial data and logs it."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the serial listener node."""
        super().__init__('serial_listener')
        
        # Timer for polling serial data
        self.timer = self.create_timer(0.1, self.read_serial_data)

    def read_serial_data(self):
        """Reads and logs data from the serial port."""
        data = self.read_serial()
        if data:
            self.get_logger().info(f"Received: {data}")
>>>>>>> REPLACE

#!/usr/bin/env python3

import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from geometry_msgs.msg import Twist
import serial
import threading
import time  # Add this line

class MotorControllerNode(Node):
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__('motor_controller')
        # Parameters
        self.declare_parameter('port', '/dev/ttyAMA2')
        self.declare_parameter('baudrate', 115200)
        self.declare_parameter('wheel_base', 0.2)
        self.declare_parameter('max_speed', 1.0)

        # Get parameters
        port = self.get_parameter('port').get_parameter_value().string_value
        baudrate = self.get_parameter('baudrate').get_parameter_value().integer_value
        self.wheel_base = self.get_parameter('wheel_base').get_parameter_value().double_value
        self.max_speed = self.get_parameter('max_speed').get_parameter_value().double_value

        # Initialize serial communication
        try:
            self.ser = serial.Serial(port, baudrate, timeout=1)
            self.get_logger().info(f"Connected to serial port {port} at {baudrate} baud.")
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Failed to open serial port {port}: {e}")
            rclpy.shutdown()
            return
=======

import rclpy

from servo_2040.serial_node import SerialNode

class MotorControllerNode(SerialNode):

        super().__init__('motor_controller')

        self.declare_parameter('max_speed', 1.0)

    def read_serial(self) -> Optional[str]:
        """Read data from the serial port.
        
        Returns:
            Optional[str]: Data read from serial port or None if error
        """
        if self.serial is None:
            self.connect_serial()
            return None
            
        try:
            if self.serial.in_waiting > 0:
                return self.serial.readline().decode('utf-8').strip()
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Serial read error: {e}")
            self.serial = None
        return None

    def __del__(self):
        """Cleanup when the node is destroyed."""
        if hasattr(self, 'serial') and self.serial is not None:
            try:
                self.serial.close()
                self.get_logger().info("Serial port closed")
            except Exception as e:
                self.get_logger().error(f"Error closing serial port: {e}")

def main():
    PORT = 8000
    # Get the installed path for the package
    web_dir = os.path.join(get_package_share_directory('wall_e_web'), 'web')
    os.chdir(web_dir)

    handler = http.server.SimpleHTTPRequestHandler
    with socketserver.TCPServer(("", PORT), handler) as httpd:
        print(f"Serving Wall-E web interface at http://localhost:{PORT}")
        httpd.serve_forever()
=======
def main():
    try:
        # Get the port from environment variable or use default
        port = int(os.getenv('WALL_E_WEB_PORT', '8000'))
        
        # Get the installed path for the package
        web_dir = os.path.join(get_package_share_directory('wall_e_web'), 'web')
        os.chdir(web_dir)

        handler = http.server.SimpleHTTPRequestHandler
        with socketserver.TCPServer(("", port), handler) as httpd:
            print(f"Serving Wall-E web interface at http://localhost:{port}")
            try:
                httpd.serve_forever()
            except KeyboardInterrupt:
                print("\nShutting down web server...")
                httpd.shutdown()
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error starting web server: {e}")
        return 1
    return 0
>>>>>>> REPLACE

    def __init__(self, node_name: str):
        """Initialize the serial node.
        
        Args:
            node_name: Name of the ROS2 node
        """
        super().__init__(node_name)
        
        # Declare common parameters with descriptions
        self.declare_parameter(
            'serial_port',
            '/dev/ttyACM0',
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Serial port to connect to'
            )
        )
        self.declare_parameter(

=======
    def read_from_pico(self):
        """Thread function to continuously read from Pico."""
        try:
            while rclpy.ok():
                data = self.read_serial()
                if data:
                    try:
                        # Log at debug level since this is frequent
                        self.get_logger().debug(f"Received from Pico: {data}")
                    except ValueError as e:
                        self.get_logger().warn(f"Invalid data from Pico: {e}")
        except Exception as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Error in read thread: {e}")
>>>>>>> REPLACE

#### great, how i can launch this?  

Let me help you set up a launch file to start all the nodes. First, we need to create a proper launch file:

src/wall_e_launch/launch/all_nodes.launch.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
from launch import LaunchDescription
from launch_ros.actions import Node

def generate_launch_description():
    """Generate launch description with all components."""
    ld = LaunchDescription()

    # Start the motor controller node
    motor_controller_node = Node(
        package='motor_controller',
        executable='motor_controller_node',
        name='motor_controller',
        parameters=[{
            'serial_port': '/dev/ttyACM0',
            'baudrate': 115200,
            'wheel_base': 0.2,
            'max_speed': 1.0
        }],
        output='screen'
    )

    # Start the serial listener node
    serial_listener_node = Node(
        package='servo_2040',
        executable='serial_listener',
        name='serial_listener',
        parameters=[{
            'serial_port': '/dev/ttyACM1',
            'baudrate': 115200
        }],
        output='screen'
    )

    # Start the web server node
    web_server_node = Node(
        package='wall_e_web',
        executable='serve_web',
        name='web_server',
        output='screen',
        parameters=[{
            'port': 8000
        }]
    )

    # Add all nodes to the launch description
    ld.add_action(motor_controller_node)
    ld.add_action(serial_listener_node)
    ld.add_action(web_server_node)

    return ld
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Now you can launch all nodes with:

```bash
ros2 launch wall_e_launch all_nodes.launch.py
```

This will start:
1. The motor controller node (listening on /dev/ttyACM0)
2. The serial listener node (listening on /dev/ttyACM1) 
3. The web interface (accessible at http://localhost:8000)

You can modify the parameters in the launch file to match your setup (like serial ports, baudrates, etc).

To test individual nodes, you can also run them separately:

```bash
ros2 run motor_controller motor_controller_node
ros2 run servo_2040 serial_listener
ros2 run wall_e_web serve_web
```

<<<<<<< SEARCH

System: Ubuntu 24.04.x

#### Installation

https://docs.ros.org/en/jazzy/Installation/Ubuntu-Install-Debs.html

source /opt/ros/jazzy/setup.bash
source ~/ros2_ws/install/setup.bash
=======
# Wall-E Robot Control System

A ROS2-based control system for a Wall-E inspired robot, featuring joystick control, motor management, and web interface monitoring.

## Overview

This project implements a complete robot control system using ROS2 Jazzy, running on Ubuntu 24.04. It includes:

- Joystick-based teleoperation using an 8BitDo Lite 2 controller
- Differential drive motor control via serial communication
- Web-based monitoring interface
- Modular node architecture for extensibility

## Tech Stack

- **OS**: Ubuntu 24.04
- **Robot Framework**: ROS2 Jazzy
- **Languages**: Python 3.12
- **Hardware**:
  - Raspberry Pi (main controller)
  - Pimoroni Servo 2040 (motor controller)
  - 8BitDo Lite 2 (bluetooth controller)

## Key Features

- Differential drive control with configurable parameters
- Bluetooth joystick integration
- Serial communication with motor controller
- Web monitoring interface
- Modular node architecture
- Parameter-based configuration

## Architecture

The system consists of several ROS2 nodes:

1. **Joy Node**: Handles joystick input
2. **Teleop Node**: Converts joystick commands to velocity commands
3. **Motor Controller Node**: Manages motor control via serial communication
4. **Serial Listener**: Monitors feedback from the motor controller
5. **Web Server**: Provides web-based monitoring interface

## Installation

1. **ROS2 Setup**:
   ```bash
   # Install ROS2 Jazzy
   https://docs.ros.org/en/jazzy/Installation/Ubuntu-Install-Debs.html

   # Source ROS2
   source /opt/ros/jazzy/setup.bash
   source ~/ros2_ws/install/setup.bash
   ```
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Readme.md
```markdown
<<<<<<< SEARCH
### Bluetooth

1. **Enable Bluetooth and Pair the Controller:**

    * **Install Bluetooth Packages:**

        ```bash
        sudo apt update
        sudo apt install bluetooth bluez blueman
        ```

    * **Start the Bluetooth Service:**

        ```bash
        sudo systemctl start bluetooth
        ```

    * **Put the Controller in Pairing Mode:**

        * Press and hold the **Start** button on your 8BitDo Lite 2 until the LEDs flash rapidly.
    * **Pair Using Bluetoothctl:**

        ```bash
        bluetoothctl
        ```

        * In the `bluetoothctl` prompt, enter:

            ```csharp
            agent on
            default-agent
            scan on
            ```

        * Wait for the controller to appear (e.g., `8BitDo Lite 2`), then note its MAC address.
        * Pair and connect:

            ```ruby
            pair XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX
            trust XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX
            connect XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX
            ```

        * Exit `bluetoothctl`:

            ```
            quit
            ```

2. **Verify the Controller is Detected:**

    * **Check for Joystick Devices:**

        ```bash
        ls /dev/input/js*
        ```

        * You should see `/dev/input/js0`.
    * **Install Joystick Utilities:**

        ```bash
        sudo apt install joystick
        ```

    * **Test the Controller:**

        ```bash
        jstest /dev/input/js0
        ```

        * Move the sticks and press buttons to ensure inputs are registered.


### Serial testing

8. **Test Access to the Serial Port:**

    * Try accessing the serial port directly:

        ```bash
        sudo apt install minicom
        minicom -D /dev/ttyAMA0
        ```

    * If the port opens without errors, it's accessible.
=======
3. **Controller Setup**:

   a. Install Bluetooth packages:
   ```bash
   sudo apt update
   sudo apt install bluetooth bluez blueman
   sudo systemctl start bluetooth
   ```

   b. Pair the 8BitDo Lite 2:
   - Hold Start button until LEDs flash
   - Use bluetoothctl:
   ```bash
   bluetoothctl
   agent on
   default-agent
   scan on
   # Wait for controller to appear
   pair XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX
   trust XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX
   connect XX:XX:XX:XX:XX:XX
   quit
   ```

4. **Verify Setup**:

   a. Check joystick:
   ```bash
   sudo apt install joystick
   ls /dev/input/js*
   jstest /dev/input/js0
   ```

   b. Test serial port:
   ```bash
   sudo apt install minicom
   minicom -D /dev/ttyAMA0
   ```

## Usage

   colcon build
   source install/setup.bash
   ```

   ```bash
   ros2 launch wall_e_launch all_nodes.launch.py

   ```bash
   ros2 run wall_e_web serve_web
   ```

## Configuration

- Joystick mapping in `config/teleop_twist_joy.yaml`
- Motor parameters in launch file
- Serial ports and baudrates in launch file
- Web server port via WALL_E_WEB_PORT environment variable

## Development

- Use `colcon build --packages-select <package>` for specific package builds
- Run `ros2 topic list` and `ros2 node list` to verify system state
- Monitor `/cmd_vel` topic for movement commands
- Check web interface at http://localhost:8000

First, let's create the new package structure:

src/wall_e/setup.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
from setuptools import setup
import os
import subprocess
from setuptools.command.install import install

package_name = 'wall_e'

class CustomInstallCommand(install):
    """Custom install command to upload firmware during colcon build."""
    def run(self):
        install.run(self)
        print("Running custom post-build step: Uploading firmware...")
        firmware_uploader = os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), 'scripts/upload_firmware.py')
        try:
            subprocess.run(['python3', firmware_uploader], check=True)
        except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
            print(f"Firmware upload failed: {e}")
            exit(1)

setup(
    name=package_name,
    version='0.0.0',
    packages=[package_name],
    data_files=[
        ('share/ament_index/resource_index/packages',
            ['resource/' + package_name]),
        ('share/' + package_name, ['package.xml']),
        ('share/' + package_name + '/launch', ['launch/all_launch.py']),
        ('share/' + package_name + '/firmware', ['firmware/main.py']),
    ],
    install_requires=['setuptools', 'pyserial', 'adafruit-ampy', 'rclpy'],
    zip_safe=True,
    maintainer='mneuhaus',
    maintainer_email='marc@neuhaus.nrw',
    description='Wall-E Robot ROS2 Package',

src/wall_e/wall_e/serial_node.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
import serial
import time
from typing import Optional


class SerialNode(Node):
    """Base class for ROS2 nodes that communicate over serial."""

    def __init__(self, node_name: str):
        """Initialize the serial node.
        
        Args:
            node_name: Name of the ROS2 node
        """
        super().__init__(node_name)
        
        # Declare common parameters with descriptions
        self.declare_parameter(
            'serial_port',
            '/dev/ttyACM0',
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Serial port to connect to'
            )
        )
        self.declare_parameter(
            'baudrate',
            115200,
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Serial baudrate'
            )
        )
        
        # Get parameters
        self.serial_port = self.get_parameter('serial_port').value
        self.baudrate = self.get_parameter('baudrate').value
        self.serial: Optional[serial.Serial] = None
        
        # Initial connection attempt
        self.connect_serial()

    def connect_serial(self) -> None:
        """Attempts to connect to the serial port."""
        while self.serial is None and rclpy.ok():
            try:
                self.serial = serial.Serial(
                    self.serial_port,
                    self.baudrate,
                    timeout=1
                )
                self.get_logger().info(
                    f"Connected to {self.serial_port} at {self.baudrate} baud."
                )
            except serial.SerialException as e:
                self.get_logger().error(
                    f"Failed to connect to {self.serial_port}: {e}"
                )
                time.sleep(1)  # Wait before retrying

    def write_serial(self, data: str) -> bool:
        """Write data to the serial port.
        
        Args:
            data: String to write to serial port
            
        Returns:
            bool: True if write successful, False otherwise
        """
        if self.serial is None:
            self.connect_serial()
            return False
            
        try:
            self.serial.write(data.encode('utf-8'))
            return True
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Serial write error: {e}")
            self.serial = None
            return False

    def read_serial(self) -> Optional[str]:
        """Read data from the serial port.
        
        Returns:
            Optional[str]: Data read from serial port or None if error
        """
        if self.serial is None:
            self.connect_serial()
            return None
            
        try:
            if self.serial.in_waiting > 0:
                return self.serial.readline().decode('utf-8').strip()
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Serial read error: {e}")
            self.serial = None
        return None
>>>>>>> REPLACE

src/wall_e/wall_e/motor_controller.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
#!/usr/bin/env python3

import rclpy
from geometry_msgs.msg import Twist
from wall_e.serial_node import SerialNode
import threading

class MotorControllerNode(SerialNode):
    """Node that controls motors via serial commands."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the motor controller node."""
        super().__init__('motor_controller')
        
        # Declare parameters with descriptions
        self.declare_parameter(
            'wheel_base',
            0.2,
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Distance between wheels in meters'
            )
        )
        self.declare_parameter(
            'max_speed',
            1.0,
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Maximum linear speed in m/s'
            )
        )
        
        # Get additional parameters
        self.wheel_base = self.get_parameter('wheel_base').value
        self.max_speed = self.get_parameter('max_speed').value

        # Subscribe to /cmd_vel
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            Twist,
            'cmd_vel',
            self.cmd_vel_callback,
            10
        )

        # Start a thread to read from the Pico
        self.read_thread = threading.Thread(target=self.read_from_pico)
        self.read_thread.daemon = True
        self.read_thread.start()

    def cmd_vel_callback(self, msg):
        self.get_logger().info(f"Received cmd_vel: linear.x={msg.linear.x}, angular.z={msg.angular.z}")
        # Convert Twist message to left and right motor speeds
        linear = msg.linear.x  # Forward/backward speed
        angular = msg.angular.z  # Rotation speed

        # Compute motor speeds (differential drive)
        left_speed = linear - (angular * self.wheel_base / 2)
        right_speed = linear + (angular * self.wheel_base / 2)

        # Scale speeds to -100 to 100
        left_speed = int(max(min(left_speed / self.max_speed * 100, 100), -100))
        right_speed = int(max(min(right_speed / self.max_speed * 100, 100), -100))

        # Send speeds to Pico
        command = f"{left_speed},{right_speed}\n"
        self.write_serial(command)

    def read_from_pico(self):
        """Thread function to continuously read from Pico."""
        try:
            while rclpy.ok():
                data = self.read_serial()
                if data:
                    try:
                        # Log at debug level since this is frequent
                        self.get_logger().debug(f"Received from Pico: {data}")
                    except ValueError as e:
                        self.get_logger().warn(f"Invalid data from Pico: {e}")
        except Exception as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Error in read thread: {e}")

def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    motor_controller_node = MotorControllerNode()
    try:
        rclpy.spin(motor_controller_node)
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        pass
    finally:
        if motor_controller_node.serial:
            motor_controller_node.serial.close()
        motor_controller_node.destroy_node()
        rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()
>>>>>>> REPLACE

import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from wall_e.serial_node import SerialNode


class SerialListener(SerialNode):
    """A ROS2 node that listens to serial data and publishes it."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the serial listener node."""
        super().__init__('serial_listener')
        
        # Timer for polling serial data
        self.timer = self.create_timer(0.1, self.read_serial_data)

    def read_serial_data(self):
        """Reads and logs data from the serial port."""
        data = self.read_serial()
        if data:
            self.get_logger().info(f"Received: {data}")


def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    node = SerialListener()
    try:
        rclpy.spin(node)
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        pass
    finally:
        if node.serial:
            node.serial.close()
        node.destroy_node()
        rclpy.shutdown()

import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
import serial
import time
from typing import Optional


class SerialNode(Node):
    """Base class for ROS2 nodes that communicate over serial."""

    def __init__(self, node_name: str):
        """Initialize the serial node.
        
        Args:
            node_name: Name of the ROS2 node
        """
        super().__init__(node_name)
        
        # Declare common parameters with descriptions
        self.declare_parameter(
            'serial_port',
            '/dev/ttyACM0',
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Serial port to connect to'
            )
        )
        self.declare_parameter(
            'baudrate',
            115200,
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Serial baudrate'
            )
        )
        
        # Get parameters
        self.serial_port = self.get_parameter('serial_port').value
        self.baudrate = self.get_parameter('baudrate').value
        self.serial: Optional[serial.Serial] = None
        
        # Initial connection attempt
        self.connect_serial()

    def connect_serial(self) -> None:
        """Attempts to connect to the serial port."""
        while self.serial is None and rclpy.ok():
            try:
                self.serial = serial.Serial(
                    self.serial_port,
                    self.baudrate,
                    timeout=1
                )
                self.get_logger().info(
                    f"Connected to {self.serial_port} at {self.baudrate} baud."
                )
            except serial.SerialException as e:
                self.get_logger().error(
                    f"Failed to connect to {self.serial_port}: {e}"
                )
                time.sleep(1)  # Wait before retrying

    def write_serial(self, data: str) -> bool:
        """Write data to the serial port.
        
        Args:
            data: String to write to serial port
            
        Returns:
            bool: True if write successful, False otherwise
        """
        if self.serial is None:
            self.connect_serial()
            return False
            
        try:
            self.serial.write(data.encode('utf-8'))
            return True
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Serial write error: {e}")
            self.serial = None
            return False

    def read_serial(self) -> Optional[str]:
        """Read data from the serial port.
        
        Returns:
            Optional[str]: Data read from serial port or None if error
        """
        if self.serial is None:
            self.connect_serial()
            return None
            
        try:
            if self.serial.in_waiting > 0:
                return self.serial.readline().decode('utf-8').strip()
        except serial.SerialException as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Serial read error: {e}")
            self.serial = None
        return None

#!/usr/bin/env python3

import rclpy
from geometry_msgs.msg import Twist
from wall_e.serial_node import SerialNode
import threading

class MotorControllerNode(SerialNode):
    """Node that controls motors via serial commands."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the motor controller node."""
        super().__init__('motor_controller')
        
        # Declare parameters with descriptions
        self.declare_parameter(
            'wheel_base',
            0.2,
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Distance between wheels in meters'
            )
        )
        self.declare_parameter(
            'max_speed',
            1.0,
            descriptor=rclpy.parameter.ParameterDescriptor(
                description='Maximum linear speed in m/s'
            )
        )
        
        # Get additional parameters
        self.wheel_base = self.get_parameter('wheel_base').value
        self.max_speed = self.get_parameter('max_speed').value

        # Subscribe to /cmd_vel
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            Twist,
            'cmd_vel',
            self.cmd_vel_callback,
            10
        )

        # Start a thread to read from the Pico (if needed)
        self.read_thread = threading.Thread(target=self.read_from_pico)
        self.read_thread.daemon = True
        self.read_thread.start()

    def cmd_vel_callback(self, msg):
        self.get_logger().info(f"Received cmd_vel: linear.x={msg.linear.x}, angular.z={msg.angular.z}")
        # Convert Twist message to left and right motor speeds
        linear = msg.linear.x  # Forward/backward speed
        angular = msg.angular.z  # Rotation speed

        # Compute motor speeds (differential drive)
        left_speed = linear - (angular * self.wheel_base / 2)
        right_speed = linear + (angular * self.wheel_base / 2)

        # Scale speeds to -100 to 100
        left_speed = int(max(min(left_speed / self.max_speed * 100, 100), -100))
        right_speed = int(max(min(right_speed / self.max_speed * 100, 100), -100))

        # Send speeds to Pico
        command = f"{left_speed},{right_speed}\n"
        self.write_serial(command)

    def read_from_pico(self):
        """Thread function to continuously read from Pico."""
        try:
            while rclpy.ok():
                data = self.read_serial()
                if data:
                    try:
                        # Log at debug level since this is frequent
                        self.get_logger().debug(f"Received from Pico: {data}")
                    except ValueError as e:
                        self.get_logger().warn(f"Invalid data from Pico: {e}")
        except Exception as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f"Error in read thread: {e}")

def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    motor_controller_node = MotorControllerNode()
    try:
        rclpy.spin(motor_controller_node)
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        pass
    finally:
        if motor_controller_node.serial:
            motor_controller_node.serial.close()
        motor_controller_node.destroy_node()
        rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()

Looking at the code, the `serial_listener.py` appears to be the node that was originally from the servo_2040 package. Let's rename it to be more descriptive of its purpose.

src/wall_e/wall_e/servo_controller.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from wall_e.serial_node import SerialNode
from std_msgs.msg import Int32MultiArray


class ServoController(SerialNode):
    """A ROS2 node that controls servos via serial commands."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the servo controller node."""
        super().__init__('servo_controller')
        
        # Subscribe to servo commands
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            Int32MultiArray,
            'servo_positions',
            self.servo_callback,
            10
        )
        
        # Timer for reading feedback
        self.timer = self.create_timer(0.1, self.read_serial_data)

    def servo_callback(self, msg):
        """Handle incoming servo position commands."""
        # Format: "S,servo_id,position\n"
        for i, position in enumerate(msg.data):
            command = f"S,{i},{position}\n"
            self.write_serial(command)
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Sent servo command: {command.strip()}")

    def read_serial_data(self):
        """Reads and logs feedback data from the servos."""
        data = self.read_serial()
        if data:
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Received servo feedback: {data}")


def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    node = ServoController()
    try:
        rclpy.spin(node)
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        pass
    finally:
        if node.serial:
            node.serial.close()
        node.destroy_node()
        rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()

# wall_e_control.launch.py

from launch import LaunchDescription
from launch.actions import IncludeLaunchDescription
from launch.launch_description_sources import PythonLaunchDescriptionSource
from launch_ros.actions import Node
from ament_index_python.packages import get_package_share_directory
import os

config_file = os.path.join(
    os.path.expanduser('~'),
    'ros2_ws',
    'src',
    'teleop_twist_joy',
    'config',
    'teleop_twist_joy.yaml'
)

def generate_launch_description():
    return LaunchDescription([
        # Start the joystick node
        Node(
            package='joy',
            executable='joy_node',
            name='joy_node',
            output='screen',
        ),
        
        # Start the teleop_twist_joy node with configuration
        Node(
            package='teleop_twist_joy',
            executable='teleop_node',
            name='teleop_node',
            output='screen',
            parameters=[config_file],
            remappings=[
                ('/cmd_vel', '/cmd_vel')  # Ensures that the command is published on /cmd_vel
            ]
        ),
        
        # Start the motor controller node
        Node(
            package='motor_controller',
            executable='motor_controller_node',
            name='motor_controller_node',
            output='screen',
            parameters=[
                {'serial_port': '/dev/ttyAMA2'},  # Adjust this if using a different serial port
                {'baudrate': 115200},
                {'wheel_base': 0.2},
                {'max_speed': 1.0}
            ]
        ),
        IncludeLaunchDescription(
            PythonLaunchDescriptionSource(
                os.path.join(
                    get_package_share_directory('servo_2040'),
                    'launch',
                    'all_launch.py'
                )
            )
        ),
    ])

src/wall_e/wall_e/serve_web.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import http.server
import socketserver
import os
from ament_index_python.packages import get_package_share_directory

def main() -> int:
    """Start the web server.
    
    Returns:
        int: Exit code (0 for success, 1 for error)
    """
    try:
        # Get the port from environment variable or use default
        port = int(os.getenv('WALL_E_WEB_PORT', '8000'))
        
        # Get the installed path for the package
        web_dir = os.path.join(get_package_share_directory('wall_e'), 'web')
        os.chdir(web_dir)

        handler = http.server.SimpleHTTPRequestHandler
        with socketserver.TCPServer(("", port), handler) as httpd:
            print(f"Serving Wall-E web interface at http://localhost:{port}")
            try:
                httpd.serve_forever()
            except KeyboardInterrupt:
                print("\nShutting down web server...")
                httpd.shutdown()
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error starting web server: {e}")
        return 1
    return 0
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

src/wall_e/web/index.html
```html
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html>
<head>
    <title>Wall-E Control</title>
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/roslib/build/roslib.min.js"></script>
</head>
<body>
    <h1>Wall-E Control Panel</h1>

    <!-- Linear Velocity Control -->
    <label>Linear Velocity:</label>
    <input type="range" id="linearVel" min="-1.0" max="1.0" step="0.1" value="0">
    <span id="linearVelValue">0</span>
    <br>

    <!-- Angular Velocity Control -->
    <label>Angular Velocity:</label>
    <input type="range" id="angularVel" min="-1.0" max="1.0" step="0.1" value="0">
    <span id="angularVelValue">0</span>
    <br><br>

    <!-- Stop Button -->
    <button id="stopButton">Stop</button>
    <br><br>

    <!-- Connection Status -->
    <div id="status">Status: Disconnected</div>

    <script>
        // Connect to ROS
        var ros = new ROSLIB.Ros({
            url: 'ws://wall-e.local:9090' // Update 'localhost' if accessing remotely
        });

        ros.on('connection', function() {
            document.getElementById('status').innerText = 'Status: Connected';
        });

        ros.on('error', function(error) {
            document.getElementById('status').innerText = 'Status: Error';
            console.error(error);
        });

        ros.on('close', function() {
            document.getElementById('status').innerText = 'Status: Disconnected';
        });

        // Create a topic for /cmd_vel
        var cmdVel = new ROSLIB.Topic({
            ros: ros,
            name: '/cmd_vel',
            messageType: 'geometry_msgs/msg/Twist'
        });

        // Publish velocity commands
        function publishVelocity(linear, angular) {
            var twist = new ROSLIB.Message({
                linear: { x: linear, y: 0, z: 0 },
                angular: { x: 0, y: 0, z: angular }
            });
            cmdVel.publish(twist);
        }

        // Update velocity from sliders
        var linearSlider = document.getElementById('linearVel');
        var angularSlider = document.getElementById('angularVel');

        linearSlider.oninput = function() {
            document.getElementById('linearVelValue').innerText = this.value;
            publishVelocity(parseFloat(this.value), parseFloat(angularSlider.value));
        };

        angularSlider.oninput = function() {
            document.getElementById('angularVelValue').innerText = this.value;
            publishVelocity(parseFloat(linearSlider.value), parseFloat(this.value));
        };

        // Stop button
        document.getElementById('stopButton').onclick = function() {
            linearSlider.value = 0;
            angularSlider.value = 0;
            document.getElementById('linearVelValue').innerText = '0';
            document.getElementById('angularVelValue').innerText = '0';
            publishVelocity(0, 0);
        };
    </script>
</body>
</html>

```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import http.server
import socketserver
import os
from ament_index_python.packages import get_package_share_directory

def main() -> int:
    """Start the web server.
    
    Returns:
        int: Exit code (0 for success, 1 for error)
    """
    try:
        # Get the port from environment variable or use default
        port = int(os.getenv('WALL_E_WEB_PORT', '8000'))
        
        # Get the installed path for the package
        web_dir = os.path.join(get_package_share_directory('wall_e'), 'web')
        os.chdir(web_dir)

        handler = http.server.SimpleHTTPRequestHandler
        with socketserver.TCPServer(("", port), handler) as httpd:
            print(f"Serving Wall-E web interface at http://localhost:{port}")
            try:
                httpd.serve_forever()
            except KeyboardInterrupt:
                print("\nShutting down web server...")
                httpd.shutdown()
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error starting web server: {e}")
        return 1
    return 0

The current location (src/teleop_twist_joy/config/teleop_twist_joy.yaml) follows ROS2 conventions where:

#### great, now lets create a new node to output sound files for wall-e  

I'll help create a new sound output node for Wall-E. We'll need to create a new Python module for the sound node. First, let me propose the new files:

src/wall_e/wall_e/sound_player.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from std_msgs.msg import String
import pygame
import os
from pathlib import Path

class SoundPlayerNode(Node):
    """ROS2 node that plays sound files based on received messages."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__('sound_player')
        
        # Initialize pygame mixer
        pygame.mixer.init()
        
        # Get the path to sound files - assuming they're in a 'sounds' directory
        self.sound_dir = Path(__file__).parent.parent / 'sounds'
        if not self.sound_dir.exists():
            self.get_logger().warn(f'Sound directory not found at {self.sound_dir}')
            
        # Create subscription
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            String,
            'wall_e/sound',
            self.sound_callback,
            10)
            
    def sound_callback(self, msg):
        """Handle incoming sound requests."""
        sound_file = self.sound_dir / f"{msg.data}.wav"
        
        if sound_file.exists():
            try:
                pygame.mixer.music.load(str(sound_file))
                pygame.mixer.music.play()
                self.get_logger().info(f'Playing sound: {sound_file.name}')
            except Exception as e:
                self.get_logger().error(f'Failed to play sound {sound_file}: {e}')
        else:
            self.get_logger().warn(f'Sound file not found: {sound_file}')

def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    node = SoundPlayerNode()
    try:
        rclpy.spin(node)
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        pass
    finally:
        node.destroy_node()
        rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()

src/wall_e/wall_e/sound_player.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
import pygame
import os
from std_msgs.msg import String

class SoundPlayerNode(Node):
    """ROS2 node that plays sound files based on received messages."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__('sound_player')
        
        # Initialize pygame mixer
        pygame.mixer.init()
        
        # Create subscription
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            String,
            'sound_request',
            self.sound_callback,
            10)
            
        self.get_logger().info('Sound player node initialized')
        
        # Sound files directory
        self.sound_dir = os.path.join(
            os.path.dirname(__file__),
            '..',
            'sounds'
        )
        
    def sound_callback(self, msg):
        """Play requested sound file."""
        sound_file = os.path.join(self.sound_dir, msg.data)
        
        if os.path.exists(sound_file):
            try:
                pygame.mixer.music.load(sound_file)
                pygame.mixer.music.play()
                self.get_logger().info(f'Playing sound: {msg.data}')
            except Exception as e:
                self.get_logger().error(f'Error playing sound {msg.data}: {str(e)}')
        else:
            self.get_logger().warning(f'Sound file not found: {msg.data}')

def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    node = SoundPlayerNode()
    rclpy.spin(node)
    node.destroy_node()
    rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()

```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
import os
import pygame

class SoundController(Node):
    """A ROS2 node that plays sound files for Wall-E."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__('sound_controller')
        
        # Initialize pygame mixer
        pygame.mixer.init()
        
        # Create a subscription for sound commands
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            String,
            'sound_command',
            self.sound_callback,
            10)
        
        self.get_logger().info('Sound controller initialized')
        
        # Directory containing sound files
        self.sound_dir = os.path.join(
            os.path.dirname(__file__), 
            '..', 
            'sounds'
        )
        
    def sound_callback(self, msg):
        """Handle incoming sound commands."""
        sound_file = os.path.join(self.sound_dir, f"{msg.data}.wav")
        
        if os.path.exists(sound_file):
            try:
                pygame.mixer.music.load(sound_file)
                pygame.mixer.music.play()
                self.get_logger().info(f'Playing sound: {msg.data}')
            except Exception as e:
                self.get_logger().error(f'Error playing sound: {str(e)}')
        else:
            self.get_logger().warning(f'Sound file not found: {sound_file}')

def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    node = SoundController()
    rclpy.spin(node)
    node.destroy_node()
    rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()

#### ok, great now i want to use the openrouter api (probably sonnet as model, but should be configurable) to integrate an llm that will act as the "soul" of wall-e, by which i mean it'll receive text input and then respond with topics to control the existing ros2 nodes  

I'll help create a new ROS2 node that will act as Wall-E's "soul" using the OpenRouter API. We'll need to:

1. Create a new soul_controller.py node
2. Update setup.py to include the new node and dependencies
3. Create a configuration file for API settings

First, let's create the new node:

src/wall_e/wall_e/soul_controller.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from std_msgs.msg import String
import aiohttp
import asyncio
import json
import os
from typing import Dict, List

class SoulController(Node):
    """Wall-E's soul - processes text input through LLM and controls other nodes."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__('soul_controller')
        
        # Load configuration
        self.config = self.load_config()
        
        # Publishers
        self.sound_publisher = self.create_publisher(String, 'sound_command', 10)
        self.motor_publisher = self.create_publisher(String, 'motor_command', 10)
        self.servo_publisher = self.create_publisher(String, 'servo_command', 10)
        
        # Subscription for text input
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            String,
            'wall_e_input',
            self.input_callback,
            10)
        
        self.get_logger().info('Soul controller initialized')
        
    def load_config(self) -> Dict:
        """Load configuration from parameters."""
        self.declare_parameters(
            namespace='',
            parameters=[
                ('openrouter_api_key', ''),
                ('model', 'sonnet'),
                ('system_prompt', (
                    'You are Wall-E, the lovable robot. '
                    'Your responses should control Wall-E\'s actions through these topics:\n'
                    '- sound_command: for playing sounds\n'
                    '- motor_command: for movement\n'
                    '- servo_command: for gestures\n'
                    'Respond with natural language and include command topics in [brackets].'
                ))
            ]
        )
        
        return {
            'api_key': self.get_parameter('openrouter_api_key').value,
            'model': self.get_parameter('model').value,
            'system_prompt': self.get_parameter('system_prompt').value
        }
    
    async def get_llm_response(self, user_input: str) -> str:
        """Get response from OpenRouter API."""
        headers = {
            'Authorization': f'Bearer {self.config["api_key"]}',
            'HTTP-Referer': 'https://github.com/yourusername/wall-e',
            'Content-Type': 'application/json'
        }
        
        data = {
            'model': self.config['model'],
            'messages': [
                {'role': 'system', 'content': self.config['system_prompt']},
                {'role': 'user', 'content': user_input}
            ]
        }
        
        try:
            async with aiohttp.ClientSession() as session:
                async with session.post(
                    'https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/chat/completions',
                    headers=headers,
                    json=data
                ) as response:
                    result = await response.json()
                    return result['choices'][0]['message']['content']
        except Exception as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f'API call failed: {str(e)}')
            return ''
    
    def extract_commands(self, response: str) -> List[Dict[str, str]]:
        """Extract commands from response text using [topic:command] format."""
        commands = []
        try:
            import re
            matches = re.findall(r'\[(.*?)\]', response)
            for match in matches:
                if ':' in match:
                    topic, command = match.split(':', 1)
                    commands.append({'topic': topic.strip(), 'command': command.strip()})
        except Exception as e:
            self.get_logger().error(f'Command extraction failed: {str(e)}')
        return commands
    
    def publish_commands(self, commands: List[Dict[str, str]]):
        """Publish extracted commands to appropriate topics."""
        for cmd in commands:
            msg = String()
            msg.data = cmd['command']
            
            if cmd['topic'] == 'sound_command':
                self.sound_publisher.publish(msg)
            elif cmd['topic'] == 'motor_command':
                self.motor_publisher.publish(msg)
            elif cmd['topic'] == 'servo_command':
                self.servo_publisher.publish(msg)
    
    def input_callback(self, msg: String):
        """Handle incoming text input."""
        loop = asyncio.get_event_loop()
        response = loop.run_until_complete(self.get_llm_response(msg.data))
        
        if response:
            self.get_logger().info(f'LLM Response: {response}')
            commands = self.extract_commands(response)
            self.publish_commands(commands)
        else:
            self.get_logger().warning('No response from LLM')

def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    node = SoulController()
    rclpy.spin(node)
    node.destroy_node()
    rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

        'rosbridge_server',
=======
    install_requires=[

        'pyserial',
        'adafruit-ampy',
        'rclpy',

        'aiohttp',
>>>>>>> REPLACE

                    '[servo_command:look_up]\n'
                    '[motor_command:forward]\n'

import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from wall_e.serial_node import SerialNode
from std_msgs.msg import Int32MultiArray


class ServoController(SerialNode):
    """A ROS2 node that controls servos via serial commands."""
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the servo controller node."""
        super().__init__('servo_controller')
        
        # Subscribe to servo commands
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            Int32MultiArray,
            'servo_positions',
            self.servo_callback,
            10
        )
        
        # Timer for reading feedback
        self.timer = self.create_timer(0.1, self.read_serial_data)

    def servo_callback(self, msg):
        """Handle incoming servo position commands."""
        # Format: "S,servo_id,position\n"
        for i, position in enumerate(msg.data):
            command = f"S,{i},{position}\n"
            self.write_serial(command)
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Sent servo command: {command.strip()}")

    def read_serial_data(self):
        """Reads and logs feedback data from the servos."""
        data = self.read_serial()
        if data:
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Received servo feedback: {data}")
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from wall_e.serial_node import SerialNode
from std_msgs.msg import String
import time
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple

class ServoController(SerialNode):
    """A ROS2 node that controls servos via serial commands for Wall-E's movements."""
    
    # Define servo IDs and their functions
    HEAD_TILT = 0    # Up/down head movement
    HEAD_PAN = 1     # Left/right head movement
    RIGHT_ARM = 2    # Right arm
    LEFT_ARM = 3     # Left arm
    EYES = 4         # Eye movement
    
    # Predefined positions for each servo (0-180 degrees)
    SERVO_POSITIONS = {
        'neutral': {
            HEAD_TILT: 90,   # Center
            HEAD_PAN: 90,    # Center
            RIGHT_ARM: 90,   # Down
            LEFT_ARM: 90,    # Down
            EYES: 90,        # Center
        },
        'look_up': {
            HEAD_TILT: 45,   # Tilted up
            HEAD_PAN: 90,    # Center
            EYES: 45,        # Looking up
        },
        'look_down': {
            HEAD_TILT: 135,  # Tilted down
            HEAD_PAN: 90,    # Center
            EYES: 135,       # Looking down
        },
        'tilt_head': {
            HEAD_TILT: 90,   # Center
            HEAD_PAN: 120,   # Tilted right
            EYES: 90,        # Center
        },
        'wave': {
            RIGHT_ARM: 180,  # Up
        },
        'hands_together': {
            RIGHT_ARM: 135,  # Forward
            LEFT_ARM: 45,    # Forward
        },
        'curious': {
            HEAD_TILT: 80,   # Slightly tilted
            HEAD_PAN: 100,   # Slightly right
            EYES: 85,        # Slightly up
        },
        'happy': {
            HEAD_TILT: 75,   # Slightly up
            EYES: 75,        # Slightly up
            RIGHT_ARM: 135,  # Partially up
            LEFT_ARM: 45,    # Partially up
        },
        'sad': {
            HEAD_TILT: 120,  # Down
            EYES: 120,       # Down
            RIGHT_ARM: 45,   # Down
            LEFT_ARM: 135,   # Down
        }
    }
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the servo controller node."""
        super().__init__('servo_controller')
        
        # Subscribe to servo commands
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            String,
            'servo_command',
            self.servo_callback,
            10
        )
        
        # Timer for reading feedback
        self.timer = self.create_timer(0.1, self.read_serial_data)
        
        # Set initial position
        self.current_positions = self.SERVO_POSITIONS['neutral'].copy()
        self.set_servo_positions(self.current_positions)
        
    def set_servo_positions(self, positions: Dict[int, int]) -> None:
        """Set multiple servo positions."""
        for servo_id, position in positions.items():
            command = f"S,{servo_id},{position}\n"
            self.write_serial(command)
            self.current_positions[servo_id] = position
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Sent servo command: {command.strip()}")
            time.sleep(0.05)  # Small delay between commands
            
    def interpolate_positions(self, start: Dict[int, int], end: Dict[int, int], 
                            steps: int = 10) -> List[Dict[int, int]]:
        """Generate interpolated positions between start and end positions."""
        positions = []
        for step in range(steps + 1):
            pos = {}
            for servo_id in start.keys():
                if servo_id in end:
                    start_pos = start[servo_id]
                    end_pos = end[servo_id]
                    pos[servo_id] = int(start_pos + (end_pos - start_pos) * (step / steps))
            positions.append(pos)
        return positions

    def execute_gesture(self, gesture_name: str) -> None:
        """Execute a predefined gesture with smooth interpolation."""
        if gesture_name not in self.SERVO_POSITIONS:
            self.get_logger().warning(f"Unknown gesture: {gesture_name}")
            return
            
        target_positions = self.SERVO_POSITIONS[gesture_name]
        
        # Create start positions from current positions
        start_positions = {servo_id: self.current_positions.get(servo_id, pos) 
                         for servo_id, pos in target_positions.items()}
        
        # Generate and execute interpolated positions
        positions = self.interpolate_positions(start_positions, target_positions)
        for pos in positions:
            self.set_servo_positions(pos)
            time.sleep(0.05)  # Adjust for smoother/faster movement

    def servo_callback(self, msg: String) -> None:
        """Handle incoming servo gesture commands."""
        gesture = msg.data.strip()
        self.get_logger().info(f"Executing gesture: {gesture}")
        self.execute_gesture(gesture)

    def read_serial_data(self):
        """Reads and logs feedback data from the servos."""
        data = self.read_serial()
        if data:
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Received servo feedback: {data}")
>>>>>>> REPLACE

#### shit, aside from the left_hand, left_wrist, left_shoulder and the same on the right are actually simple motors and not servos, we need a seperate controller for those i guess  

I'll help create a separate motor controller for the arms and update the servo controller. We'll need to:

src/wall_e/wall_e/arm_controller.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from wall_e.serial_node import SerialNode
from std_msgs.msg import String
import time
from typing import Dict

class ArmController(SerialNode):
    """A ROS2 node that controls Wall-E's arm motors via serial commands."""
    
    # Define motor IDs and their functions
    LEFT_HAND = 0    # Left hand gripper (open/close)
    LEFT_WRIST = 1   # Left wrist rotation
    LEFT_SHOULDER = 2  # Left shoulder joint
    RIGHT_HAND = 3   # Right hand gripper (open/close)
    RIGHT_WRIST = 4  # Right wrist rotation
    RIGHT_SHOULDER = 5 # Right shoulder joint
    
    # Predefined positions/movements
    MOTOR_POSITIONS = {
        'neutral': {
            LEFT_HAND: 0,      # Released
            LEFT_WRIST: 90,    # Center
            LEFT_SHOULDER: 90, # Neutral
            RIGHT_HAND: 0,     # Released
            RIGHT_WRIST: 90,   # Center
            RIGHT_SHOULDER: 90 # Neutral
        },
        'wave': {
            RIGHT_SHOULDER: 135, # Raised
            RIGHT_WRIST: 180,   # Rotated up
            RIGHT_HAND: 0,      # Open
        },
        'hands_together': {
            LEFT_SHOULDER: 45,   # Forward
            LEFT_WRIST: 90,     # Center
            LEFT_HAND: 50,      # Partially closed
            RIGHT_SHOULDER: 135, # Forward
            RIGHT_WRIST: 90,    # Center
            RIGHT_HAND: 50,     # Partially closed
        },
        'grab': {
            LEFT_HAND: 100,     # Closed
            RIGHT_HAND: 100,    # Closed
        },
        'release': {
            LEFT_HAND: 0,       # Open
            RIGHT_HAND: 0,      # Open
        }
    }
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the arm controller node."""
        super().__init__('arm_controller')
        
        # Subscribe to arm commands
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            String,
            'arm_command',
            self.arm_callback,
            10
        )
        
        # Timer for reading feedback
        self.timer = self.create_timer(0.1, self.read_serial_data)
        
        # Set initial position
        self.current_positions = self.MOTOR_POSITIONS['neutral'].copy()
        self.set_motor_positions(self.current_positions)
        
    def set_motor_positions(self, positions: Dict[int, int]) -> None:
        """Set multiple motor positions."""
        for motor_id, position in positions.items():
            command = f"M,{motor_id},{position}\n"
            self.write_serial(command)
            self.current_positions[motor_id] = position
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Sent motor command: {command.strip()}")
            time.sleep(0.05)  # Small delay between commands

    def execute_movement(self, movement_name: str) -> None:
        """Execute a predefined arm movement."""
        if movement_name not in self.MOTOR_POSITIONS:
            self.get_logger().warning(f"Unknown movement: {movement_name}")
            return
            
        target_positions = self.MOTOR_POSITIONS[movement_name]
        self.set_motor_positions(target_positions)

    def arm_callback(self, msg: String) -> None:
        """Handle incoming arm movement commands."""
        movement = msg.data.strip()
        self.get_logger().info(f"Executing arm movement: {movement}")
        self.execute_movement(movement)

    def read_serial_data(self):
        """Reads and logs feedback data from the motors."""
        data = self.read_serial()
        if data:
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Received motor feedback: {data}")


def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    node = ArmController()
    try:
        rclpy.spin(node)
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        pass
    finally:
        if node.serial:
            node.serial.close()
        node.destroy_node()
        rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()
>>>>>>> REPLACE

#### since the motors of the arm don't have an encoder we can't set some specific degree for them, we can only acuate the motor in clockwise or counter clockwise direction for a specific amount of time, the motors itself are "loosly" coupled and will simply skip if there is too much resistance, so we can't count on a specific position for any of those motors  

I'll help modify the arm controller to work with time-based motor control instead of positions. We'll need to:

1. Update the motor commands to use direction and duration
2. Change the predefined movements to use timing
3. Modify the command structure

Here are the changes:

src/wall_e/wall_e/arm_controller.py
```python

    # Define motor IDs and their functions
    LEFT_HAND = 0    # Left hand gripper (open/close)
    LEFT_WRIST = 1   # Left wrist rotation
    LEFT_SHOULDER = 2  # Left shoulder joint
    RIGHT_HAND = 3   # Right hand gripper (open/close)
    RIGHT_WRIST = 4  # Right wrist rotation
    RIGHT_SHOULDER = 5 # Right shoulder joint
    
    # Predefined positions/movements
    MOTOR_POSITIONS = {
        'neutral': {
            LEFT_HAND: 0,      # Released
            LEFT_WRIST: 90,    # Center
            LEFT_SHOULDER: 90, # Neutral
            RIGHT_HAND: 0,     # Released

            RIGHT_SHOULDER: 90 # Neutral
        },

```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    def set_motor_positions(self, positions: Dict[int, int]) -> None:
        """Set multiple motor positions."""
        for motor_id, position in positions.items():
            command = f"M,{motor_id},{position}\n"
            self.write_serial(command)
            self.current_positions[motor_id] = position
            self.get_logger().debug(f"Sent motor command: {command.strip()}")
            time.sleep(0.05)  # Small delay between commands

    def execute_movement(self, movement_name: str) -> None:
        """Execute a predefined arm movement."""
        if movement_name not in self.MOTOR_POSITIONS:
            self.get_logger().warning(f"Unknown movement: {movement_name}")
            return
            
        target_positions = self.MOTOR_POSITIONS[movement_name]
        self.set_motor_positions(target_positions)
=======
    def run_motor(self, motor_id: int, direction: int, duration_ms: int) -> None:
        """Run a motor in specified direction for given duration."""
        command = f"M,{motor_id},{direction},{duration_ms}\n"
        self.write_serial(command)
        self.get_logger().debug(f"Sent motor command: {command.strip()}")
        time.sleep(duration_ms / 1000.0)  # Wait for movement to complete

    def execute_movement(self, movement_name: str) -> None:
        """Execute a predefined arm movement sequence."""
        if movement_name not in self.MOTOR_SEQUENCES:
            self.get_logger().warning(f"Unknown movement: {movement_name}")
            return
            
        sequence = self.MOTOR_SEQUENCES[movement_name]
        for motor_id, direction, duration in sequence:
            self.run_motor(motor_id, direction, duration)

#### could we extract the `SERVO_POSITIONS` and `MOTOR_SEQUENCES` into a seperate controller, since it could make sence to have combined sequences that involve motors and servos  

I'll help create a new sequence controller and modify the existing controllers to use it. Here are the changes:

1. First, let's create a new sequence controller:

src/wall_e/wall_e/sequence_controller.py
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
=======
import rclpy
from rclpy.node import Node
from std_msgs.msg import String
import time
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple

class SequenceController(Node):
    """Controls sequences of servo and motor movements for Wall-E."""
    
    # Servo IDs
    BELLY_DOOR = 0      # Front compartment door
    NECK_RAISE = 1      # Neck up/down (0-90)
    NECK_TILT = 2       # Neck tilt (0-90)
    NECK_PAN = 3        # Neck left/right (0-180)
    HEAD_LEFT = 4       # Left eye raise (0-40)
    EYEBROW_LEFT = 5    # Left eyebrow (0-90)
    HEAD_RIGHT = 6      # Right eye raise (0-40)
    EYEBROW_RIGHT = 7   # Right eyebrow (0-90)
    
    # Motor IDs
    LEFT_HAND = 0       # Left hand gripper
    LEFT_WRIST = 1      # Left wrist rotation
    LEFT_SHOULDER = 2   # Left shoulder joint
    RIGHT_HAND = 3      # Right hand gripper
    RIGHT_WRIST = 4     # Right wrist rotation
    RIGHT_SHOULDER = 5  # Right shoulder joint
    
    # Motor directions
    CW = 1  # Clockwise
    CCW = 0 # Counter-clockwise
    
    # Predefined servo positions
    SERVO_POSITIONS = {
        'neutral': {
            BELLY_DOOR: 0,      # Closed
            NECK_RAISE: 45,     # Middle position
            NECK_TILT: 45,      # Middle position
            NECK_PAN: 90,       # Center
            HEAD_LEFT: 20,      # Slightly raised
            EYEBROW_LEFT: 45,   # Neutral
            HEAD_RIGHT: 20,     # Slightly raised
            EYEBROW_RIGHT: 45,  # Neutral
        },
        'look_up': {
            NECK_RAISE: 20,     # Raised
            NECK_TILT: 30,      # Tilted back
            HEAD_LEFT: 30,      # Eyes up
            HEAD_RIGHT: 30,     # Eyes up
            EYEBROW_LEFT: 60,   # Raised
            EYEBROW_RIGHT: 60,  # Raised
        },
        'look_down': {
            NECK_RAISE: 70,     # Lowered
            NECK_TILT: 60,      # Tilted forward
            HEAD_LEFT: 10,      # Eyes down
            HEAD_RIGHT: 10,     # Eyes down
            EYEBROW_LEFT: 30,   # Lowered
            EYEBROW_RIGHT: 30,  # Lowered
        },
        'tilt_head': {
            NECK_TILT: 30,      # Tilted
            NECK_PAN: 120,      # Turned right
            HEAD_LEFT: 25,      # Slight raise
            HEAD_RIGHT: 15,     # Lower than left
            EYEBROW_LEFT: 60,   # Raised
            EYEBROW_RIGHT: 30,  # Lowered
        },
        'curious': {
            NECK_RAISE: 40,     # Slightly raised
            NECK_TILT: 30,      # Tilted
            NECK_PAN: 100,      # Slightly right
            HEAD_LEFT: 30,      # Raised
            HEAD_RIGHT: 30,      # Raised
            EYEBROW_LEFT: 70,   # Raised high
            EYEBROW_RIGHT: 70,  # Raised high
        },
        'happy': {
            NECK_RAISE: 30,     # Raised
            HEAD_LEFT: 35,      # Raised high
            HEAD_RIGHT: 35,     # Raised high
            EYEBROW_LEFT: 80,   # Raised high
            EYEBROW_RIGHT: 80,  # Raised high
        },
        'sad': {
            NECK_RAISE: 60,     # Lowered
            NECK_TILT: 60,      # Looking down
            HEAD_LEFT: 10,      # Lowered
            HEAD_RIGHT: 10,     # Lowered
            EYEBROW_LEFT: 20,   # Drooped
            EYEBROW_RIGHT: 20,  # Drooped
        },
        'open_belly': {
            BELLY_DOOR: 90,     # Open
        },
        'close_belly': {
            BELLY_DOOR: 0,      # Closed
        }
    }
    
    # Predefined motor sequences
    MOTOR_SEQUENCES = {
        'wave': [
            (RIGHT_SHOULDER, CW, 1000),   # Raise shoulder
            (RIGHT_WRIST, CW, 500),       # Rotate wrist up
            (RIGHT_WRIST, CCW, 500),      # Rotate back
            (RIGHT_SHOULDER, CCW, 1000),  # Lower shoulder
        ],
        'hands_together': [
            (LEFT_SHOULDER, CCW, 800),    # Move left forward
            (RIGHT_SHOULDER, CW, 800),    # Move right forward
            (LEFT_HAND, CW, 500),         # Close left hand
            (RIGHT_HAND, CW, 500),        # Close right hand
        ],
        'grab': [
            (LEFT_HAND, CW, 1000),        # Close left gripper
            (RIGHT_HAND, CW, 1000),       # Close right gripper
        ],
        'release': [
            (LEFT_HAND, CCW, 1000),       # Open left gripper
            (RIGHT_HAND, CCW, 1000),      # Open right gripper
        ]
    }
    
    # Combined sequences (servo positions and motor movements)
    COMBINED_SEQUENCES = {
        'greet': [
            {'type': 'servo', 'name': 'look_up'},
            {'type': 'motor', 'name': 'wave'},
            {'type': 'servo', 'name': 'happy'},
        ],
        'collect': [
            {'type': 'servo', 'name': 'look_down'},
            {'type': 'motor', 'name': 'grab'},
            {'type': 'servo', 'name': 'neutral'},
        ],
        'store': [
            {'type': 'servo', 'name': 'open_belly'},
            {'type': 'motor', 'name': 'hands_together'},
            {'type': 'servo', 'name': 'close_belly'},
        ]
    }
    
    def __init__(self):
        """Initialize the sequence controller node."""
        super().__init__('sequence_controller')
        
        # Publishers for other controllers
        self.servo_publisher = self.create_publisher(String, 'servo_command', 10)
        self.arm_publisher = self.create_publisher(String, 'arm_command', 10)
        
        # Subscription for sequence commands
        self.subscription = self.create_subscription(
            String,
            'sequence_command',
            self.sequence_callback,
            10
        )
        
        self.get_logger().info('Sequence controller initialized')
    
    def execute_sequence(self, sequence_name: str) -> None:
        """Execute a combined sequence of movements."""
        if sequence_name in self.COMBINED_SEQUENCES:
            sequence = self.COMBINED_SEQUENCES[sequence_name]
            for action in sequence:
                if action['type'] == 'servo':
                    msg = String()
                    msg.data = action['name']
                    self.servo_publisher.publish(msg)
                elif action['type'] == 'motor':
                    msg = String()
                    msg.data = action['name']
                    self.arm_publisher.publish(msg)
                time.sleep(0.5)  # Allow time for movement to complete
        else:
            self.get_logger().warning(f'Unknown sequence: {sequence_name}')
    
    def sequence_callback(self, msg: String) -> None:
        """Handle incoming sequence commands."""
        sequence = msg.data.strip()
        self.get_logger().info(f'Executing sequence: {sequence}')
        self.execute_sequence(sequence)


def main(args=None):
    rclpy.init(args=args)
    node = SequenceController()
    try:
        rclpy.spin(node)
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        pass
    finally:
        node.destroy_node()
        rclpy.shutdown()

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

            'sound_controller = wall_e.sound_controller:main',
            'soul_controller = wall_e.soul_controller:main',

    # Define motor IDs and their functions
    LEFT_HAND = 0    # Left hand gripper
    LEFT_WRIST = 1   # Left wrist rotation
    LEFT_SHOULDER = 2  # Left shoulder joint
    RIGHT_HAND = 3   # Right hand gripper
    RIGHT_WRIST = 4  # Right wrist rotation
    RIGHT_SHOULDER = 5 # Right shoulder joint
    
    # Motor directions
    CW = 1  # Clockwise
    CCW = 0 # Counter-clockwise
    
    # Predefined movements with timing (motor_id, direction, duration_ms)
    MOTOR_SEQUENCES = {
        'wave': [
            (RIGHT_SHOULDER, CW, 1000),   # Raise shoulder
            (RIGHT_WRIST, CW, 500),       # Rotate wrist up
            (RIGHT_WRIST, CCW, 500),      # Rotate back
            (RIGHT_SHOULDER, CCW, 1000),  # Lower shoulder
        ],

            (RIGHT_HAND, CW, 1000),       # Close right gripper

        'release': [
            (LEFT_HAND, CCW, 1000),       # Open left gripper
            (RIGHT_HAND, CCW, 1000),      # Open right gripper
        ]

    RIGHT_HAND = SequenceController.RIGHT_HAND
    RIGHT_WRIST = SequenceController.RIGHT_WRIST

>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

These changes:
1. Create a new SequenceController that manages all predefined positions and sequences
2. Move servo positions and motor sequences into the SequenceController
3. Add combined sequences that mix servo and motor movements
4. Update the existing controllers to use the definitions from SequenceController
5. Add sequence publishing to the soul controller

The soul controller can now use combined sequences like:
```
[sequence_command:greet]  # Wave and look happy
[sequence_command:collect]  # Look down and grab something
[sequence_command:store]  # Store item in belly compartment
```

#### well the sequence controller should not be concerned with the actual pins, those should be in the motor, arm and servo controller  

You're right - let's move the hardware-specific pin definitions to their respective controller files and keep the sequence controller focused on sequences. I'll make the necessary changes:

These changes resolve the circular import issues by:
1. Having hardware definitions in their respective controllers
2. Having the sequence controller import and use those definitions
3. Having the sequence controller define all sequences
4. Having the motor and servo controllers get their sequences from the sequence controller at runtime through ROS2 messages

The sequence controller becomes the central place for defining sequences while respecting the hardware abstractions in each controller.

Readme.md
```python
<<<<<<< SEARCH
## Configuration

- Joystick mapping in `config/teleop_twist_joy.yaml`
- Motor parameters in launch file
- Serial ports and baudrates in launch file
- Web server port via WALL_E_WEB_PORT environment variable
=======
## Configuration

### Hardware Connections

#### Servo 2040 Pinout
- **Servos**:
  - Pin 0: Belly Door (0-90°)
  - Pin 1: Neck Raise (0-90°)
  - Pin 2: Neck Tilt (0-90°)
  - Pin 3: Neck Pan (0-180°)
  - Pin 4: Head Left (0-40°)
  - Pin 5: Eyebrow Left (0-90°)
  - Pin 6: Head Right (0-40°)
  - Pin 7: Eyebrow Right (0-90°)

- **Motors**:
  - Pins 8/9: Left Hand (Motor + Direction)
  - Pins 10/11: Left Wrist (Motor + Direction)
  - Pins 12/13: Left Shoulder (Motor + Direction)
  - Pins 14/15: Right Hand (Motor + Direction)
  - Pins 16/17: Right Wrist (Motor + Direction)
  - Pins 18/19: Right Shoulder (Motor + Direction)

#### Serial Connection
- Connect Servo 2040 UART to Raspberry Pi:
  - Servo 2040 TX → Pi RX (GPIO 15)
  - Servo 2040 RX → Pi TX (GPIO 14)
  - GND → GND

### Software Configuration

#### OpenRouter Setup
1. Create account at [OpenRouter](https://openrouter.ai/)
2. Get API key from dashboard
3. Set environment variable:
   ```bash
   export OPENROUTER_API_KEY='your_api_key_here'
   ```
4. Or add to your `~/.bashrc`:
   ```bash
   echo 'export OPENROUTER_API_KEY="your_api_key_here"' >> ~/.bashrc
   source ~/.bashrc
   ```

#### Other Settings
- Joystick mapping in `config/teleop_twist_joy.yaml`
- Motor parameters in launch file
- Serial ports and baudrates in launch file
- Web server port via WALL_E_WEB_PORT environment variable
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

#### What's wrong? Fix  

The error indicates that the device `/dev/ttyUSB0` is not accessible. This could be because:
1. The device isn't connected
2. The user doesn't have permissions to access it
3. The device name is incorrect

Let's modify the Makefile to:
1. Add a permission check/fix step
2. Add better error handling
3. List available ports

Makefile
```makefile
<<<<<<< SEARCH
# Variables
USB_PORT = /dev/ttyUSB0      # Default USB port for MicroPython board
PYTHON_FILE = install/servo_2040/share/servo_2040/firmware/main.py         # Python script to upload

# Flash command using ampy
flash: $(PYTHON_FILE)
	ampy --port $(USB_PORT) put $(PYTHON_FILE)
=======
# Variables
USB_PORT = /dev/ttyUSB0      # Default USB port for MicroPython board
PYTHON_FILE = install/servo_2040/share/servo_2040/firmware/main.py         # Python script to upload

# Flash command using ampy
flash: check-port $(PYTHON_FILE)
	@echo "Flashing $(PYTHON_FILE) to $(USB_PORT)..."
	ampy --port $(USB_PORT) put $(PYTHON_FILE)

# Check if port exists and fix permissions if needed
check-port:
	@echo "Checking port $(USB_PORT)..."
	@if [ ! -e $(USB_PORT) ]; then \
		echo "Error: $(USB_PORT) not found. Available ports:"; \
		ls -l /dev/ttyUSB* 2>/dev/null || echo "No USB ports found"; \
		ls -l /dev/ttyACM* 2>/dev/null || echo "No ACM ports found"; \
		exit 1; \
	fi
	@if [ ! -w $(USB_PORT) ]; then \
		echo "Fixing permissions for $(USB_PORT)..."; \
		sudo chmod a+rw $(USB_PORT); \
	fi
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

First try running:
```bash
ls -l /dev/ttyUSB* /dev/ttyACM*
```
This will show what serial ports are available. Then you can either:

1. Fix permissions:
```bash
sudo chmod a+rw /dev/ttyUSB0
```

2. Or add yourself to the dialout group:
```bash
sudo usermod -a -G dialout $USER
```
(Note: This requires logging out and back in to take effect)

Then try the flash command again:
```bash
make flash
```
